  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_af58d16d-4301-42a8-9cf2-ed307a2d10ec'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11777945933993547507">Here we meet Horatio Hornblower, a young man of 17, in this Volume #1 of what becomes the 11 volume set about the career of this British Naval officer fighting against Napoleon and his tyranny of Europe as an inexperienced midshipman in January 1794. Bullied and forced into a duel, he takes an even chance. And then he has many more chances to show his skills and ingenuitie</span>
  <span id="freeText11777945933993547507" style="display:none">Here we meet Horatio Hornblower, a young man of 17, in this Volume #1 of what becomes the 11 volume set about the career of this British Naval officer fighting against Napoleon and his tyranny of Europe as an inexperienced midshipman in January 1794. Bullied and forced into a duel, he takes an even chance. And then he has many more chances to show his skills and ingenuities - from sailing a ship full of wetted and swelling rice to imprisonment and saving the lives of shipwrecked sailors. And along the way, he fights galleys, feeds cattle, stays out of the way of the guillotine, and makes friends with a Duchess. Here Hornblower becomes a man and develops the strength of character which will make him a hero to his men, and to all England.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11777945933993547507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2424764922" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2424764922" />
    <a title="Fergus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70395042-fergus"><img alt="Fergus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567548184p2/70395042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2424764922?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fergus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fergus" href="/user/show/70395042-fergus">Fergus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2424764922" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16077053722515299414">When I was growing up, my Mom, who doubled as the village librarian, URGED me to read this book. I’m sure she saw in me a little Midshipman Hornblower.<br/><br/>Shy, standoffish, and predisposed to dumb clumsiness, I obviously needed the role model of a misfit like I was who would bloom under the rigours of his first command.<br/><br/>But being slightly autistic I was averse to authoritarian posturing.<br/><br/>Later, though, I would be plunged into the thick of it as Head Boy of our new high school. Why me???<br/><br/>Popularity? Not</span>
  <span id="freeText16077053722515299414" style="display:none">When I was growing up, my Mom, who doubled as the village librarian, URGED me to read this book. I’m sure she saw in me a little Midshipman Hornblower.<br /><br />Shy, standoffish, and predisposed to dumb clumsiness, I obviously needed the role model of a misfit like I was who would bloom under the rigours of his first command.<br /><br />But being slightly autistic I was averse to authoritarian posturing.<br /><br />Later, though, I would be plunged into the thick of it as Head Boy of our new high school. Why me???<br /><br />Popularity? Not a chance. <br /><br />Looks? A blank on that score too - I was a bit overweight and ungainly. <br /><br />But lady luck has doggedly plodded close behind me all my long life!<br /><br />And besides - when I was a kid I was much more intent on doing what the other kids liked to do: have fun and joke around.<br /><br />When I finally picked up this book, nearly 60 years later, I was as unfit as ever to read it - for a different reason.<br /><br />You see, I’ve always believed in a still slightly autistic adulthood that virtue, and not swagger and a strutting attitude, yields the best rewards. <br /><br />I’ve seen too many intellectual flyweights and moral midgets assume the reins of command in my long career, and through their draconian attitudes, fake the whole thing passably enough.<br /><br />That’s the strong and unpleasant impression I got from Hornblower’s first acts after being promoted, particularly in the flintlock duel scene.<br /><br />So when I reread this, Horatio, I decided not to Friend you. <br /><br />***<br />However, it’s a wonderfully well-written book and a good yarn - and you know what? After reading Jason Koivu’s beautiful five-star review here on GR, I’ve decided to someday (if I get the chance) revisit it!<br /><br />So why’s that? <br /><br />Well, back in the times when I was similarly “in command” of a group of office workers, I led by intuition and not by will - much like the young, untried ordinary seaman Hornblower.<br /><br />So his embarrassing moments reminded me too much of my own. Real Aspie Territory.<br /><br />Too many folks I know have corrupted their youth early on with the strategy of power, its dark secrets veiled in a “tedious argument of insidious intent” to lead their hapless victims to an “overwhelming question” and force their hands. <br /><br />For what indeed is a truly Ingenuous Youth, if not a series of embarrassments - which includes a hearty helping of humiliation at the hands of these dark early bloomers?<br /><br />And what is ‘presence’ to us, if not swagger? We others are simply continually weathering the storms seeded by these conniving cognoscenti - ad infititum. And should we not add here that this thing called ‘presence’ is really only a Gnostic Presence?<br /><br />For into such dark checkmates were the plans of the moral flyweights I knew in my career intended to lead their victims!<br /><br />So we Ingenuous Ones have no choice but to keep dancing...<br /><br />But I see in Jason’s review that his character develops what used to be called traditional “presence” - that same confidence in himself to which I was only a newcomer in my late middle age, when I saw its moral and religious roots clearly.<br /><br />And if Hornblower and I turn out to be dancing to the same sheet of music, it will be worthwhile to revisit this book.<br /><br />So, dear readers: <br /><br />Please consider this review as very much a Work in Progress.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16077053722515299414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11993320787534596714" style="display:none">I’ve got really strong memories of enjoying the Hornblower TV movies of the late 90’s, so seemed like another perfect book series to get started with. <br />I’d decided to read these in chronological order.<br /><br />Whilst there is a slight prequel feel to these adventures, it’s definitely the best place to start.<br />Seeing young 17-year-old Hornblower’s inexperience helps the reader to understand the nautical terms with ease and get a greater sense of the late Eighteenth Century setting.<br />I definitely could sympathise with his seasickness!<br /><br />There’s a real short story collection vibe to this volume, with some parts more interesting than others.<br />But ultimately it’s seeing the young Horatio grow throughout the tales that makes this a great adventures novel.</span>

<div id="review_38427796" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38427796" />
    <a title="Jason Koivu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu"><img alt="Jason Koivu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560521450p2/1742824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38427796?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38427796" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15127961914352296189"><i>Mr. Midshipman Hornblower</i> begins the seafaring career of a young British officer in one of the greatest historical naval fiction series ever penned! It's a heck of a fun rollick with seamen!<br/><br/><i>Horatio Hornblower commences his career in the Royal Navy as an inexperienced midshipman in January 1794. Through a series of challenges and adventures both in and out of combat, Hornblower discovers he is actually talented in both seamanship and leadership.</i> - Wikipedia<br/><br/>This initial book in the series reads so</span>
  <span id="freeText15127961914352296189" style="display:none"><i>Mr. Midshipman Hornblower</i> begins the seafaring career of a young British officer in one of the greatest historical naval fiction series ever penned! It's a heck of a fun rollick with seamen!<br><br><i>Horatio Hornblower commences his career in the Royal Navy as an inexperienced midshipman in January 1794. Through a series of challenges and adventures both in and out of combat, Hornblower discovers he is actually talented in both seamanship and leadership.</i> - Wikipedia<br><br>This initial book in the series reads somewhat episodic, with whole creating a rounded introductory. The first chapter, "Hornblower and the Even Chance," is a fantastically tense and dynamic way to begin. <br><br>A bit of a Mary Sue, Hornblower seems to do no wrong much of the time. He is given the slightest of character flaws and he occasionally fails, but his fairly consistent successes and need to chastise himself for his failings could get a bit tedious for some readers. On the other hand, isn't it nice when the good guy wins?<br><br>The funny thing about <i>Mr. Midshipman Hornblower</i> is that it's a prequel. Forester went back and began his series after he'd already brought the narrative to completion. When he originally started writing these books, he began Hornblower's naval career in media res. After getting to the end, he went back and wrote a handful of prequels, sort of like what goddamned George Lucas did with Star Wars. However, in this case the creator's craft had improved. The writing in <i>Mr. Midshipman Hornblower</i> has a better flow to it, an effortless ease. The characters feel more like real people. I have to say, it's funny to get into the middle of the entire series and encounter the old books with their stiff characters and stilted writing. <br><br>Regardless of any shortcomings, the series is still one of my favorites and this is a great send off to a wonderful voyage!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461700138i/18899279._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>A far too dashing image of Ioan Gruffudd, who played Hornblower in the tv series</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15127961914352296189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_42029206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42029206" />
    <a title="Werner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/903390-werner"><img alt="Werner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216337931p2/903390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42029206?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Werner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Werner" href="/user/show/903390-werner">Werner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of &quot;sailing-ship navy&quot; yarns</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42029206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3949882744446642261">Both my oldest daughter and her husband are fans of the Hornblower series, and I've thoroughly enjoyed the A & E movie productions that I've seen of the Hornblower corpus; so I was motivated to read the books, and decided to begin at the beginning of Hornblower's career, with this novel. (My only previous acquaintance with Forester was from reading one of his short stories.) I'm glad to say it didn't disappoint!<br/><br/>Forester had a deft hand with maritime adventure (not all of it dealing with combat),</span>
  <span id="freeText3949882744446642261" style="display:none">Both my oldest daughter and her husband are fans of the Hornblower series, and I've thoroughly enjoyed the A &amp; E movie productions that I've seen of the Hornblower corpus; so I was motivated to read the books, and decided to begin at the beginning of Hornblower's career, with this novel. (My only previous acquaintance with Forester was from reading one of his short stories.) I'm glad to say it didn't disappoint!<br /><br />Forester had a deft hand with maritime adventure (not all of it dealing with combat), characterization, and easily-readable Realist style. The movies based on parts of this novel don't always follow the book very closely; the Hornblower revealed here is a more complex character than the film version, younger (a teen at the beginning) and more callow, and definitely fallible. I could actually identify with him to a high degree --even though I'd never be able to do some of the things he did-- because he's portrayed as awkward and shy, and as pushing himself to the limit to do things that tax and scare him mainly because he fears other people's ridicule if he doesn't; and because he can make the same kind of absent-minded mistakes (like forgetting to cock his pistol when he's going into combat) that I could imagine myself making. One critic I've read felt that Forester is a less deep writer than his fellow maritime novelist, Melville, because he doesn't go in for symbolism and allegory. Nonetheless, his writing isn't shallow; he confronts his hero with several demands for moral decision-making. (And on these occasions, Hornblower comes through, earning the reader's respect and setting a good example.) The writing here is vivid; you get a really powerful picture of the hard and dangerous character of naval life in that day as you experience, along with the hero, the palms of his hands being flayed bloody by having to slide down a rough rope from a falling mast, or the winter cold and wet of the waves constantly breaking over him in an open boat.<br /><br />Although this book is usually considered a novel, the structure is episodic enough that it could have been billed as a collection of short stories; though the chapters are placed in chronological order, they're each perfectly self-contained and could stand as distinct units. Since this wasn't the first Hornblower book to be written, it doesn't furnish any detailed information about his life before he went to sea, or why he decided on such a career; I'm assuming this would have appeared in the first book, but the lack of it here made for a gap in the character development. Also, if Forester ever explained the basic nautical terms of a sail-driven ship and its rigging and operations, he doesn't do it here; technical terms are used abundantly and you glean (or sometimes, don't glean) an approximation of the meaning from the context, unless you've picked up a definition elsewhere. (A sailing ship entry in a good visual dictionary would be a useful accompaniment to this read!) But these are minor caveats; I'm looking forward to eventually reading the next two books (in terms of Hornblower's life chronology) of the series, at least.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3949882744446642261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1264261748" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1264261748" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1264261748?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio 9780792778462" href="/book/show/16369391-mr-midshipman-hornblower">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1audio">1audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=3series">3series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1264261748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16013947639933453819">My library didn't have this when I started reading the series, so I wound up reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77040.Lieutenant_Hornblower__Hornblower_Saga_Chronological_Order___2_' title='Lieutenant Hornblower (Hornblower Saga Chronological Order, #2) by C.S. Forester' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lieutenant Hornblower</a>, the second book chronologically, before this. There was quite a difference in the two books. Where 'Lieutenant' was pretty much one long story with a short bit tacked on to the end, 'Midshipman' jumps from one short adventure to another like a frog on a hot road, but I liked both. Reading them out of order wasn't a huge deal, although I would have preferred to read them in chronological or</span>
  <span id="freeText16013947639933453819" style="display:none">My library didn't have this when I started reading the series, so I wound up reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77040.Lieutenant_Hornblower__Hornblower_Saga_Chronological_Order___2_" title="Lieutenant Hornblower (Hornblower Saga Chronological Order, #2) by C.S. Forester" rel="nofollow noopener">Lieutenant Hornblower</a>, the second book chronologically, before this. There was quite a difference in the two books. Where 'Lieutenant' was pretty much one long story with a short bit tacked on to the end, 'Midshipman' jumps from one short adventure to another like a frog on a hot road, but I liked both. Reading them out of order wasn't a huge deal, although I would have preferred to read them in chronological order &amp; will do so from now on. I have all 11 books.<br /><br />Hornblower is a really interesting hero. He's not physically perfect. He's tough as nails, but shy, skinny, prone to seasickness, &amp; clumsiness. He's fairly smart &amp; does his best thinking with real problems under life-threatening circumstances, but most of all, he has a very rigid code of honor &amp; holds true to it. He never prevaricates, even to himself &amp; this series of adventures shows off the entire young man.<br /><br />Hornblower is rather offhand about the many hardships a sailor faced in the British Navy of the early 1800's. I thought back to my Army days &amp; tried to put it in perspective. Each man had 22" to hang his hammock. Imagine that for a moment. That's about shoulder width &amp; that's the room they had, not only to sleep in, but to get in &amp; out of the bloody thing! Suddenly my WWII barracks with rows of bunk beds seemed quite spacious.<br /><br />Why so little room? Forester mentions 300 men on a 'frigate' &amp; space issues in several places. What's a frigate &amp; how big is it? I looked around a little &amp; guess it was about 135' long x 40' wide. (Tough to tell since the term seems to have covered a lot of different types &amp; sizes.) Figure 2 decks &amp; the math shows that each man had 36 square feet, a 6'x6' area without allowing for any superstructure, bracing, tapering, cannon, supplies, or anything else which may well have eaten up a lot of the room. Oh my! Tight quarters indeed, especially for voyages of months. They might have more room in a grave. <br /><br />Even with all the fresh sea air, I imagine the smell was enough to knock a vulture over. Barely mentioned are the 'latrines' which weren't really, as such. They were an area with ropes strung off the side of the ship. They swung out over the ocean with their trousers down &amp; hung on while they did their business, no matter what the weather was like. Ugh!<br /><br />Food &amp; water are mentioned a few times. Do NOT look it up. It's enough to gag a maggot. And there were rats. Yet Hornblower likes the sea life! It's beyond imagining. Shore life must have been dismal indeed. It makes the adventures &amp; hardships that he willingly endures far more believable. <br /><br />I'm still quite entranced by the series &amp; will continue to listen to it. It's very well read, a perfect medium.<br /><br />The full series in Published Order:<br />1. The Happy Return (1937) aka Beat to Quarters<br />2. The Ship of the Line (1938)<br />3. Flying Colours (1938)<br />4. The Commodore (1945) aka Commodore Hornblower<br />5. Lord Hornblower (1946)<br />6. Mr Midshipman Hornblower (1950)<br />7. Lieutenant Hornblower (1952)<br />8. Hornblower and the Atropos (1953)<br />9. Admiral Hornblower in the West Indies (1957)<br />10. Hornblower and the Hotspur (1962)<br />11. Hornblower and the Crisis (1967) aka Hornblower During the Crisis (partial, unfinished novel)<br />12. Hornblower Addendum (2011)<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6668650.Hornblower_One_More_Time" title="Hornblower One More Time by C.S. Forester" rel="nofollow noopener">Hornblower One More Time</a> contains 3 short stories:<br />- Hand of Destiny<br />- Charitable Offering aka The Bad Samaritan<br />- Hornblower and His Majesty<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11684374.Hornblower_Addendum___Five_Stories__Hornblower_Saga_" title="Hornblower Addendum - Five Stories (Hornblower Saga) by C.S. Forester" rel="nofollow noopener">Hornblower Addendum - Five Stories</a> (2011) is 5 adventures of Horatio Hornblower, two as Lieutenant, two as Captain, and one as Admiral of the Fleet.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/84762.The_Hornblower_Companion" title="The Hornblower Companion by C.S. Forester" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hornblower Companion</a> is an atlas with brief descriptons &amp; should be read along with the books.<br /><br /><b>Hornblower Chronology:</b> From Wikipedia &amp; other sources.<br />(SS = Short Story)<br /><br />1. Mr Midshipman Hornblower Jan 1794–Mar 1798<br />1.4 Hornblower and the Hand of Destiny (SS) 1798 (need to find)<br />1.5 Hornblower and the Big Decision (Temptation or Widow McCool) (SS) 1799<br />2. Lieutenant Hornblower May 1800–Mar 1803<br />3. Hornblower and the Hotspur Apr 1803–Jul 1805<br />4. Hornblower and the Crisis aka Hornblower During the Crisis Aug 1805–Dec 1805 (partial, unfinished novel)<br />5. Hornblower and the Atropos Dec 1805–Jan 1808<br />6. The Happy Return aka Beat to Quarters Jun 1808–Oct 1808<br />7. The Ship of the Line May 1810–Oct 1810<br />7.5 Hornblower's Charitable Offering aka The Bad Samaritan (SS) Jun 1810<br />8. Flying Colours Nov 1810–Jun 1811<br />8.5 Hornblower and His Majesty (SS) 1812<br />9. The Commodore aka Commodore Hornblower Apr 1812–Dec 1812<br />10. Lord Hornblower Oct 1813–Jun 1814<br />11. Admiral Hornblower in the West Indies May 1821–Oct 1823<br />11.5 The Last Encounter (SS) Nov 1848<br /><br />"The Point and the Edge" is a brief outline of a story.<br /><br />The <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horatio_Hornblower" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia entry for the series</a> has a lot of good information, but careful of spoilers. There is a table listing all the books &amp; stories with both the UK/USA published names &amp; dates, plus the chronological dates, movies &amp; other stuff.<br /><br />See Joy's review for movies:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1281792277">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16013947639933453819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4685357636138991232">Here we have a lad of seventeen, a greenhorn deckhand, who works his way up through the ranks with his determination, grit, and a dash of book learnin': poor, seasick Hornblower, who barely manages to escape with his life from the duel he himself orchestrated, knowing his own inability and lack of experience in combat! Here we have Mr. Midshipman Hornblower of the HMS Indefatigable, unaware of the dangers of a leaky ship with a cargo hold full of dry rice! Here we have the pertinacious, the teme</span>
  <span id="freeText4685357636138991232" style="display:none">Here we have a lad of seventeen, a greenhorn deckhand, who works his way up through the ranks with his determination, grit, and a dash of book learnin': poor, seasick Hornblower, who barely manages to escape with his life from the duel he himself orchestrated, knowing his own inability and lack of experience in combat! Here we have Mr. Midshipman Hornblower of the HMS Indefatigable, unaware of the dangers of a leaky ship with a cargo hold full of dry rice! Here we have the pertinacious, the temerarious, the au courant, the über-prescient Horatio f___ing Hornblower!, foiling mutinous plots, fighting baddies on sea <i>and</i> on land, farting in the general direction of the French, Spanish, et cetera, and basically drop kicking evil in the face!<br /><br />Sometimes I forget that reading can be so <i>fun</i>. I spend a lot of my reading time struggling through dense prose, trying to understand philosophical jargon or, in the case of my recent Ulysses failure, trying to understand anything at all. Which is good. It's valuable. But <i>holy cow monkeys</i> do I enjoy hearing about Horatio Hornblower's adventures on the high sea! </span>

<div id="review_227324161" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227324161" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227324161?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=high-seas-adventures">high-seas-adventures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227324161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5171127618237636505">So, this is actually a prequel, written many years after Horatio Hornblower first took the stage and even after he had become one of England’s most famous heroes. But I’ve decided to read these in chronological order and I’m quite glad that I did. <br/><br/>In this book, Horatio is a very young midshipman (although not as young as the wealthy and titled lads who take up that position). He’s been given his first commission aboard the Justinian, where he immediately becomes known as the midshipman who got s</span>
  <span id="freeText5171127618237636505" style="display:none">So, this is actually a prequel, written many years after Horatio Hornblower first took the stage and even after he had become one of England’s most famous heroes. But I’ve decided to read these in chronological order and I’m quite glad that I did. <br /><br />In this book, Horatio is a very young midshipman (although not as young as the wealthy and titled lads who take up that position). He’s been given his first commission aboard the Justinian, where he immediately becomes known as the midshipman who got seasick while still anchored at port. He’s introverted, awkward, gangly, and a bit of a math nerd. However, what makes Horatio’s fumbles so incredibly enjoyable is the tangible affection that C.S. Forester so obviously feels for him. You can really feel Forester’s warmth and humor as Horatio contemplates suicide with all the drama of a seventeen year old, or disguises his skinny calves with a bit of wood and some plaster, or gets flustered by a questionable Duchess.<br /><br />And then there are the little glimpses of Hornblower, the leader: the man who should not be trifled with. These are even more enjoyable. Underneath all that skinny awkwardness lies a daring, brave, and rigidly honorable man. <br /><br />I’ve listened to a few author-narrated audiobooks recently, and while they weren’t terrible (and were also undoubtedly more authentic in terms of the author’s “vision”), this audiobook really reminded me of how much I love a skilled, professional narrator. The narrator for this audiobook is amazing with voices, accents, and inflections. I highly recommend this on audio.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Bob Dylan – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=o_Hc0TDBR3s" rel="nofollow noopener">When the Ship Comes In</a><br /><br />Yes, I know that this is a metaphorical “ship coming in.” But still. I think that this song is a bit about revenge, but also a bit about the inevitability of social growth and change.<br /><br />I found myself very amused by Hornblower’s unquestioning participation in government sanctioned kidnapping (“press gangs”) or piracy (“privateering”), and the casual racism that he applies to both the French and Spanish sailors, even as he looks on the practice of using galley slaves with disgust. But near the end of the book, he seems to become more open-minded and level-headed. So there! Even in a metaphorical sense, this song applies.<br /><br />And in a literal sense, obviously. Yay for high-seas adventures!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5171127618237636505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_698290576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/698290576" />
    <a title="Mr. Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15984059-mr-matt"><img alt="Mr. Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401911574p2/15984059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/698290576?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mr. Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mr. Matt" href="/user/show/15984059-mr-matt">Mr. Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15984059-mr-matt?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15984059-mr-matt?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15984059-mr-matt?shelf=ships-of-the-line">ships-of-the-line</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer698290576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7485907624916839391">Having finished the first one, I have no idea why I'd put off reading these books for years. This book was great - historical fiction/Ships of the Line/Age of Sail done right! <br/><br/>Mr. Midhsipman Hornblower introduces us to Hornblower. He boards his first ship as a raw, inexperienced and frightened midshipman at seventeen. And the book takes Honrblower and the reader on all sorts of adventures. He engages in a duel to earn his place on the ship. He is given charge (and loses) a prize ship. He visits </span>
  <span id="freeText7485907624916839391" style="display:none">Having finished the first one, I have no idea why I'd put off reading these books for years. This book was great - historical fiction/Ships of the Line/Age of Sail done right! <br /><br />Mr. Midhsipman Hornblower introduces us to Hornblower. He boards his first ship as a raw, inexperienced and frightened midshipman at seventeen. And the book takes Honrblower and the reader on all sorts of adventures. He engages in a duel to earn his place on the ship. He is given charge (and loses) a prize ship. He visits (and almost gets stuck in) Morocco. He meets a Duchess. He is captured. Throughout it all, he keeps a level head and makes the best of his situation.<br /><br />What strikes me about these books as opposed to some of the recent Age of Sail (or Age of Sail in space) fiction that I've recently read is that Hornblower faces adversity. Hornblower is given tasks and he fails! When Hornblower loses the prize ship (and his first independent command) because swelling rice in the hold literally pops his ship open from the inside out I was hooked. In too many stories of this ilk, the main character faces only token cardboard opposition - an unruly crew that needs to be whipped into shape, or some such. In this book the curve balls lobbed at Hornblower are often either self-inflicted or out of his control. That's a nice change of pace.<br /><br />Four stars out of five. The book moves along at a good pace, with plenty of action. It's a short, but fun read. My only real knock on the book is that Hornblower can be a bit of a twit. He always does the right thing. I'd like to see a little more edge on him, but that's OK. (We see a glimpse of a darker side in the next book, which is good.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="7485907624916839391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78651060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11128512176663672660">The Hornblower books by C. S. Forester are among the iconic novels of the English language, and with good reason in my opinion. I almost gave this a 4 star rating (because of my "stingy" with the 5 star ratings rule. After all 5 is the best you can give...how many can there be? But...)but decided I really do like these books to a 5 star level and they are very well written.<br/><br/>This was not the first Hornblower book...not the first written that is, but it is the first in chronological order in Hornbl</span>
  <span id="freeText11128512176663672660" style="display:none">The Hornblower books by C. S. Forester are among the iconic novels of the English language, and with good reason in my opinion. I almost gave this a 4 star rating (because of my "stingy" with the 5 star ratings rule. After all 5 is the best you can give...how many can there be? But...)but decided I really do like these books to a 5 star level and they are very well written.<br /><br />This was not the first Hornblower book...not the first written that is, but it is the first in chronological order in Hornblower's life. This book starts out with an extremely unsure and YOUNG Midshipman Hornblower arriving at his first ship. It follows him through a series of adventures from the misery of serving under a senior Midshipman who will never be promoted (because he's failed the Lieutenant's test too many times). This man takes his wretchedness and bitterness out on all the younger (thus junior)Midshipmen. The book's story continues with Hornblower's life through his promotion to Lieutenant (while he's in a Spanish prison as a prisoner of war). The book ends with his release from prisoner of war status and a promise of more adventure.<br /><br />This (these) book (books) are well worth reading. Patrick O'Brian's works have become very well known of late, in my opinion as action and adventure stories Forester's works are far superior. <br /><br />Just me of course.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11128512176663672660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_35863997" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35863997" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1134884-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475111927p2/1134884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/35863997?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/1134884-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Scott by: </span>
      Helene Brown / Dana Cattani
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1134884-scott?shelf=ships">ships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1134884-scott?shelf=1950s">1950s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1134884-scott?shelf=regency">regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1134884-scott?shelf=war">war</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35863997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15861337121616119806"><i>"Hell!" said Hornblower, actually stamping his feet on the upper gangway in his anger. "Hell <b>and</b> damnation!"</i><br/><br/>C. S. Forester's <i>Mr. Midshipman Hornblower</i> (1950) finds himself all too often frustrated in a "savage, merciless world," where he is "very much alone ... depressed, and unhappy." It's a world where very little goes as Hornblower plans: each adventurous episode nearly ends his career – and his life. The young midshipman tempers his exasperation by relying on his keen, mathematical intellect</span>
  <span id="freeText15861337121616119806" style="display:none"><i>"Hell!" said Hornblower, actually stamping his feet on the upper gangway in his anger. "Hell <b>and</b> damnation!"</i><br /><br />C. S. Forester's <i>Mr. Midshipman Hornblower</i> (1950) finds himself all too often frustrated in a "savage, merciless world," where he is "very much alone ... depressed, and unhappy." It's a world where very little goes as Hornblower plans: each adventurous episode nearly ends his career – and his life. The young midshipman tempers his exasperation by relying on his keen, mathematical intellect that's quick to appraise risks and make split-second decisions. But without friends, without family, and faced with cruel discipline, bullying, and the brutality of war, the inexperienced Hornblower grows callous, shoring up his many insecurities through violence, rigid obedience to authority, and a bravado that borders on suicidal. <br /><br />For many chapters, <i>Mr. Midshipman Hornblower</i> is a fairly dark read. Written in the gloomy days just after WWII, when Britons watched the Empire being dismantled, Forester's tale mirrors the angst and anger of the period; at the same time, though, it looks back longingly on the Empire in its first "finest hour," when – like the heroic airmen who saved England during the Blitz – courageous British seamen stood alone against a Europe dominated by an aggressive dictator.<br /><br />I was equally charmed and repelled by Forester's vulnerable, volatile midshipman; but what remained constant were my curiosity to see what became of him and the pleasure I found reading about his adventures. Fortunately for us, Forester tells a good yarn from stem to stern. While the structure of each episodic chapter is formulaic and the focus rarely strays from Hornblower, Forester's clever imagination and extensive research create a believable illusion of life in the British navy during the Napoleonic wars. There's plenty of suspense and adventure; and the grim, understated humor that liberally seasons the yarns keep the reader's spirits up and the pages turning. I had no problem finishing the book, and at the conclusion, I was happy to see the more humane, more confident lieutenant Hornblower set to embark on an illustrious maritime career. I'm looking forward to setting sail with him again soon.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15861337121616119806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1674012" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1674012" />
    <a title="Siria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/115473-siria"><img alt="Siria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332731316p2/115473.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1674012?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siria" href="/user/show/115473-siria">Siria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115473-siria?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115473-siria?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115473-siria?shelf=british-fiction">british-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1674012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1734297972851984387">This wasn't the first of the Hornblower novels to be written, but chronologically it comes first in the series of novels covering his life. For someone who is just coming to the series, this mightn't be the best place to start.<br/><br/>Although you are introduced to Hornblower as a nervous young seventeen-year-old midshipman, the fact that the book is actually comprised of a dozen or so loosely connected short stories means that the flow is rather choppy. If you are coming to the series after seeing the </span>
  <span id="freeText1734297972851984387" style="display:none">This wasn't the first of the Hornblower novels to be written, but chronologically it comes first in the series of novels covering his life. For someone who is just coming to the series, this mightn't be the best place to start.<br /><br />Although you are introduced to Hornblower as a nervous young seventeen-year-old midshipman, the fact that the book is actually comprised of a dozen or so loosely connected short stories means that the flow is rather choppy. If you are coming to the series after seeing the A&amp;E movies, as I am, it's interesting to see the stories which inspired the miniseries, but somewhat disconcerting to see the differences in characterisation. I really can see why the producers of the miniseries decided that it was necessary to add a foil for Horatio in the form of Archie Kennedy; in the books, he is so incredibly cold and neurotically repressed that it is hard to warm to him. The fact that each story in this volume only took up only twenty or so pages also meant that it suffered, in my mind, in comparison with the television movies - Kitty Cobham, for example, does not come to life in the book in the way that she does on-screen.<br /><br />The historical detail, however, is spot on, as are all the nautical details; and you can always rely on Forrester to deliver a rollicking good adventure story. I think as a stylist and a writer, though, Patrick O' Brian will always pip him as the best writer of historical naval fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1734297972851984387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1605444223" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1605444223" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4086118-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567611029p2/4086118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1605444223?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/4086118-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780241955505" href="/book/show/13320463-mr-midshipman-hornblower">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=england">england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=nautical">nautical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=spain">spain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=napoleonic-wars">napoleonic-wars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1605444223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10895473317380072961">Now that I have run out of Patrick O’Brian’s series and dabbled with several Alexander Kent’s Bolitho as a poor substitute, I took a chance to go back to the series from my youth that really turned me on to reading. I figured I would find Forrester’s starting version of the Brit navy in the Napoleanic Wars would be just be an adventurous potboiler appropriate to satisfy my twelve-year old mind. But I was surprised at the subtlety of tales, the lack of crass derring-do, and the self-effacing good</span>
  <span id="freeText10895473317380072961" style="display:none">Now that I have run out of Patrick O’Brian’s series and dabbled with several Alexander Kent’s Bolitho as a poor substitute, I took a chance to go back to the series from my youth that really turned me on to reading. I figured I would find Forrester’s starting version of the Brit navy in the Napoleanic Wars would be just be an adventurous potboiler appropriate to satisfy my twelve-year old mind. But I was surprised at the subtlety of tales, the lack of crass derring-do, and the self-effacing good humor as much as anguish with which he faced early mistakes from inexperience. <br /><br />After an apprenticeship with a captain and ship of has-beens and wimps, he gets a chance at important mentorship under a brilliant, dashing captain of the <i>Indefatigable</i> on blockade duty in the Bay of Biscay. He is so successful in taking merchant and French naval prizes, Hornblower gets his first chance of command of a ship, tasked with taking it to England with a small crew. I loved to see him overcome his sense of inadequacy and learn to juggle all the tasks of navigation, keeping authority over his seamen, and keeping watch on the prisoners. Disaster happens from his own mistakes, and he pulls off a miracle save. When the captain doesn’t punish him, he finds a way to punish himself. <br /><br />This book is composed of diverse kinds of episodes, none with the melodramatic battles I sort of expected from dim memories. The successes for him are not so much in vanquishing the major enemy ships, but in using his wits and budding leadership to save the day in terms of surviving a storm in a small boat, saving Spanish naval victims of a shipwreck on a reef, and climbing a mast in the dark to release the sail of an enemy ship assaulted by stealth in “cutting out” operation. I seem to remember Forrester painting the French and Spanish as simply despicable and treacherous, but I didn’t see much of that here in the times when he was a prisoner of their navy. The painting of the evils of slavery in the Spanish colonies and captured slave ships was a different story. <br /><br />The growth in Hornblower’s character was satisfying to experience, though in retrospect I can see how each episode was used just for that purpose, imbued with moral lessons as much as a steps on the path to the wise and courageous commander he will become. I didn’t realize this tour of his midshipmen phase was written as a prequel to a set of five that took him from lieutenant to squadron commodore. I read and loved all ten. In contrast, O’Brian puts in a lot more gritty realism in his tales, engages you more in the microcosm of the society aboard ship, and makes the friendship between his officer hero Jack Aubrey and doctor/spy/naturalist Stephen Maturin the core of his stories. But second best is pretty good. If you try the Hornblower series, see if your library has <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/84762.The_Hornblower_Companion" title="The Hornblower Companion by C.S. Forester" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hornblower Companion</a>, which provides maps for every episode and outlines the big picture on the wars and interludes between them in the period from 1794 to 1823.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10895473317380072961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_35573244" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35573244" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/35573244?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=nautical">nautical</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35573244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1553552994401310979">I may have liked this more than it deserved because I read it around the birth of our third child (Katya is two days old as I write this), but whatever the reason, I really had a good time with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/84748.Mr__Midshipman_Hornblower__Book_1_of_the_Hornblower_Saga_' title='Mr. Midshipman Hornblower (Book 1 of the Hornblower Saga) by C.S. Forester' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mr. Midshipman Hornblower</a>.<br/><br/>Better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12542.Bernard_Cornwell' title='Bernard Cornwell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cornwell</a>'s Richard Sharpe books, but not as good as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5600.Patrick_O_Brian' title='Patrick O'Brian' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patrick O'Brian</a>'s Aubrey/Maturin books, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/84748.Mr__Midshipman_Hornblower__Book_1_of_the_Hornblower_Saga_' title='Mr. Midshipman Hornblower (Book 1 of the Hornblower Saga) by C.S. Forester' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mr. Midshipman Hornblower</a> is really a novel of short stories. "<i>Hornblower</i> and the Examination for Lieutenant" and "<i>Hornblower</i> the Duchess, and the Devil" were my two favourite </span>
  <span id="freeText1553552994401310979" style="display:none">I may have liked this more than it deserved because I read it around the birth of our third child (Katya is two days old as I write this), but whatever the reason, I really had a good time with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/84748.Mr__Midshipman_Hornblower__Book_1_of_the_Hornblower_Saga_" title="Mr. Midshipman Hornblower (Book 1 of the Hornblower Saga) by C.S. Forester" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Midshipman Hornblower</a>.<br /><br />Better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12542.Bernard_Cornwell" title="Bernard Cornwell" rel="nofollow noopener">Cornwell</a>'s Richard Sharpe books, but not as good as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5600.Patrick_O_Brian" title="Patrick O'Brian" rel="nofollow noopener">Patrick O'Brian</a>'s Aubrey/Maturin books, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/84748.Mr__Midshipman_Hornblower__Book_1_of_the_Hornblower_Saga_" title="Mr. Midshipman Hornblower (Book 1 of the Hornblower Saga) by C.S. Forester" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Midshipman Hornblower</a> is really a novel of short stories. "<i>Hornblower</i> and the Examination for Lieutenant" and "<i>Hornblower</i> the Duchess, and the Devil" were my two favourite tales, but all of them were readable and kept my interest.<br /><br />I am looking forward to reading a Hornblower novel rather than a series of Hornblower stories. I think an extended tale in the Hornblower saga would be more compelling. The little details when action is at a minimum, the relationships on board ship, those are the things that really interest me. I felt that Hornblower's years as a Midshipman were covered too fast, and there were times when the jumps in his career -- from action to action -- left gaps I wish were filled. I am probably just spoiled by the stories of Jack Aubrey and Stephen Maturin, though. I'll get over it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1553552994401310979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2526197988" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2526197988" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75007576-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603216002p2/75007576.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2526197988?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/75007576-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/36911572-mr-midshipman-hornblower">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75007576-rose?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2526197988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5451584846397346395">Well, this was fun! I preferred it to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77430.Master_and_Commander__Aubrey___Maturin___1_' title='Master and Commander (Aubrey & Maturin, #1) by Patrick O'Brian' rel='nofollow noopener'>Master and Commander</a> by far. Horatio Hornblower is just a teenaged midshipman here, an intelligent and sensitive overthinker who sort of reminds me of a shy, grumpy puppy. Even though he would be mortified and offended to hear it. He's just so self-conscious and burdened despite all of his natural ability.<br/><br/>I kept wondering, how could I relate so much to an 18th century midshipman in the Royal Navy? I am not a boy. And definitely not a surly, reserved, sort-of</span>
  <span id="freeText5451584846397346395" style="display:none">Well, this was fun! I preferred it to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77430.Master_and_Commander__Aubrey___Maturin___1_" title="Master and Commander (Aubrey &amp; Maturin, #1) by Patrick O'Brian" rel="nofollow noopener">Master and Commander</a> by far. Horatio Hornblower is just a teenaged midshipman here, an intelligent and sensitive overthinker who sort of reminds me of a shy, grumpy puppy. Even though he would be mortified and offended to hear it. He's just so self-conscious and burdened despite all of his natural ability.<br /><br />I kept wondering, how could I relate so much to an 18th century midshipman in the Royal Navy? I am not a boy. And definitely not a surly, reserved, sort-of-dashing English boy. I don't get captured by French galleons, or dine with Spanish sea captains, or smuggle intelligence for British admirals.<br />But then I realized that Horatio's first job is like everyone's first job! I mean, minus the threat of grapeshot to the throat.<br /><br />You're technically an adult though you certainly don't feel like one, everyone is older than you, you feel out of your depth, are sometimes miserable, and sometimes triumphant. Some of your co-workers are a little crazy, but others are great. You pretend to know how to do things. And eventually you actually learn how to do them. It's me! It's you! It's Horatio!<br /><br />This book is episodic, so we get the full range of Hornblower's early years; narrow escapes from enemy ships, embarrassing losses, painful battles of the French Revolution, triumphant maneuvering, and some personal bitterness. If you have a craving for naval historical fiction then I highly recommend this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5451584846397346395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2845243515" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2845243515" />
    <a title="E.B. Dawson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47448891-e-b-dawson"><img alt="E.B. Dawson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595804950p2/47448891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2845243515?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="E.B. Dawson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="E.B. Dawson" href="/user/show/47448891-e-b-dawson">E.B. Dawson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47448891-e-b-dawson?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2845243515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8496436406636616636">I very much enjoy maritime fiction, when done well. This book was somehow not what I was expecting and I find it difficult to define, but I very much enjoyed it. <br/><br/>First of all, it seemed a bit more like a string of incidents rather than one cohesive story. The only thing really tying it together was that it covers the Midshipman years for Hornblower. It would have been fun to see a more substantial, carefully crafted arc for Hornblower or to see the stories tied together into a significant plot, </span>
  <span id="freeText8496436406636616636" style="display:none">I very much enjoy maritime fiction, when done well. This book was somehow not what I was expecting and I find it difficult to define, but I very much enjoyed it. <br /><br />First of all, it seemed a bit more like a string of incidents rather than one cohesive story. The only thing really tying it together was that it covers the Midshipman years for Hornblower. It would have been fun to see a more substantial, carefully crafted arc for Hornblower or to see the stories tied together into a significant plot, but honestly I didn't mind too much once I knew what to expect. <br /><br />Some of the subject matter and scenes Forester chooses to show are just unexpected. He deals with topics you don't necessarily expect to see in this genre, from Hornblower's deep depression at the beginning of the book, to the rat gambling, to the slave galleys of Spain, to the fraudulent Duchess offering to hide his despatches in her undergarments. XD XD <br /><br />The last chapter and adventure was unequivocally my favorite. Loved the descriptions of the stormy ocean coast and Hornblower's decisions are so honorable. He has been honorable throughout the book, but this truly was the culmination of that. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8496436406636616636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_552552187" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/552552187" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9172443-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335806350p2/9172443.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/552552187?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/9172443-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9172443-chris?shelf=europe">europe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9172443-chris?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9172443-chris?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9172443-chris?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9172443-chris?shelf=britain">britain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9172443-chris?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9172443-chris?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9172443-chris?shelf=hornblower">hornblower</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9172443-chris?shelf=spain">spain</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer552552187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10819370210927342113">In Horatio Hornblower, C.S. Forester created one of the most flawed heroes in military fiction. And not flawed in the "rogue" sort of way, like Richard Sharpe, but in a deeply human way. He does not strike you as a capable military officer; but he is undoubtedly brilliant, and an excellent commander. He is tone-deaf, awkward, shy, self-critical, self-doubting, and even prone to seasickness (something strange for a career naval officer). I think this, above anything else, is what makes him so app</span>
  <span id="freeText10819370210927342113" style="display:none">In Horatio Hornblower, C.S. Forester created one of the most flawed heroes in military fiction. And not flawed in the "rogue" sort of way, like Richard Sharpe, but in a deeply human way. He does not strike you as a capable military officer; but he is undoubtedly brilliant, and an excellent commander. He is tone-deaf, awkward, shy, self-critical, self-doubting, and even prone to seasickness (something strange for a career naval officer). I think this, above anything else, is what makes him so appealing. When viewed from a 3rd part narrator, as he is in some of the novels through Leftenant Bush, he seems cold and aloof, but when you are inside his brain, it is a shocking counterpoint.<br /><br />In this particular book, the first chronologically (though not the first written), Hornblower begins his naval career as a Midshipman. This book is essentially a series of short stories, recounting his progress in ability and experience, up to his promotion to full Leftenant. It gives an interesting view into the world of early 19th century naval warfare (or at least naval life, there isn't a ton of actual warfare), and sets the character up well.<br /><br />This is one of those rare times when the prequel/origin story is actually something I recommend people start with. It lets you get a handle on him earlier, and makes him more sympathetic and understandable in later books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10819370210927342113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_850608334" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/850608334" />
    <a title="Earl Grey Tea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4841374-earl-grey-tea"><img alt="Earl Grey Tea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296563240p2/4841374.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/850608334?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Earl Grey Tea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Earl Grey Tea" href="/user/show/4841374-earl-grey-tea">Earl Grey Tea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841374-earl-grey-tea?shelf=british-literature">british-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841374-earl-grey-tea?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer850608334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9269803732685390967">To be honest, I was fascinating by 18th century European navies when I was a high school student. I found the idea of man-of-wars and frigates hitting each other with cannon fire at close range while marines storm the deck of the opposing ship absolutely thrilling. My father, upon learning of my peculiar interest, bought this book for me to read. I read the it, appreciated it, but found myself having a difficult time getting the through all of the archaic, obsolete and specific naval terminology</span>
  <span id="freeText9269803732685390967" style="display:none">To be honest, I was fascinating by 18th century European navies when I was a high school student. I found the idea of man-of-wars and frigates hitting each other with cannon fire at close range while marines storm the deck of the opposing ship absolutely thrilling. My father, upon learning of my peculiar interest, bought this book for me to read. I read the it, appreciated it, but found myself having a difficult time getting the through all of the archaic, obsolete and specific naval terminology, along with a writing style that akin the Victorian style.<br /><br />Now 15 some odd years later, I found this series in the eBook format, so I decided to give them another try. This time around I am older, a bit wiser, and have much more reading experience under my belt. I was able to enjoy the stories and even remember some of the scenes from the first time I read the book as a teenager. The language and writing style didn't hinder me as much as before, but it still wasn't smooth sailing (sorry for the nautical pun in this review). This isn't a book that an average modern American reader can just sit back and enjoy on a lazy afternoon. Instead, one must dedicate a fair amount of brain processing power to navigate (sorry!) the text written in the early 19th century British style in a world that revolved around naval battles. One drowsy evening after a long day at work, the large amount of words to describe naval vessels became confusing and I lost track which English boat the Spanish galley sunk. The next morning after a refreshing night's sleep, I was able to quickly sort out which boat was which and finished the story fully understanding what had happened in the naval engagement.<br /><br />I really did enjoy reading all of the different adventures of Mr. Hornblower. Even though each story was in chronological order, it didn't follow a uniformed pattern. Chapters could be separated by a couple of months or a plethora. Even within one of the stories, over two years passed from beginning to ending. One story in particular aroused a juvenile excitement in me while I read about the military discipline and martial exploits of British regulars in the skirmishes against French soldiers. In addition to this, it was nice to read about a protagonist that was a cut above everybody else but still made mistakes. This wasn't a story about a uebermensch that does everything perfectly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9269803732685390967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
